The Chosen View: School of Ta'lim and the Structure of Nazar
Commentary explaining the addition of 'school of ta'lim' and the matter-form structure of nazar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the commentator added 'school of ta'lim' and how nazar involves matter and form.

Core Idea
Nazar has two parts: the sciences as matter, the arrangement as form.

In this passage, the commentator clarifies why the phrase 'school of ta'lim' was added to the matn. He prevents a common misunderstanding about the division of nazar into valid and invalid, and then reveals the analogy that sciences serve as matter for thought while their arrangement is its form.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and translation once to get the flow. Notice the commentator's explanation for the addition.
2
Understand the misunderstanding prevented
Identify that the phrase 'school of ta'lim' is added to prevent the assumption that the division of nazar depends on its definition as arrangement.
The chosen view includes both arrangement and acquisition.
3
Grasp the matter-form analogy
Learn that nazar requires sciences arranged in a specific form: sciences are matter, arrangement is form, leading to definition or proof.
The form is the specific arrangement that yields knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ولما كان المختار عند المتأخرين مذهب أهل التعليم، وهو أنه ترتيب العلوم عبارة المتن هكذا ولما كان المختار أنه ترتيب العلوم فزاد الشارح قوله مذهب أهل التعليم إشارة إلى دفع ما يتوهم من ظاهر عبارتہ من ابتناء انقسام النظر إلى الصحيح والفاسد على تفسيره بالترتيب كما ذكره شارح المقاصد ، ووجه الدفع الذي أشار إليه هو أن ليس مراده جعل الانقسام المذكور مبنياً على تفسيره بالترتيب حتى لا يجري على تفسير آخر على القول بالاكتساب، بل مراده أن المختار عند المتأخرين لما كان مذهب أهل التعليم وهو القول بالترتيب والاكتساب دون مذهب من يرى النظر مجرد التوجه إلى المطلوب من غير استعانة بمعلومات كما سبق، وبعد وضوح المقصود لا يبالي بما في عبارة المتن من أدني مسامحة، واعلم أن النظر سواء جعلناه نفس الترتيب أو الحركة المفضية إليه يستدعي علوما مرتبة على هيئة مخصوصة الموصل منها إلى التصور معرفاً وإلى التصديق دليلاً، ويكون العلوم أي الأمور الحاضرة مادة لذلك الموصل، والهيئة المخصوصة صورة له وقد يضافان إلى النظر بهده الملابسة، وهذا معنى كلام المصنف أن لكل ترتيب مادة وصورة وإلا فتلك العلوم وتلك الهيئة خارجتان عن الفكر قطعاً، وبهذا يظهر وجه ما يقال : إن العلوم التي يقع فيها الترتيب بمنزلة المادة للفكر، والهيئة المترتبة عليه بمنزلة الصورة، وأما ذكره الشارح في حواشي المطالع وحاشيته الصغرى توجيهاً لذلك
His statement: 'And since the chosen [view] among the later scholars is the school of ta'lim, which is that it is an arrangement of sciences' – the text of the matn is like this: 'And since the chosen [view] is that it is an arrangement of sciences', so the commentator added his statement 'the school of ta'lim' as an indication to repel what might be imagined from the apparent meaning of his phrase that the division of nazar into valid and invalid is based on its interpretation as arrangement, as mentioned by the commentator of al-Maqasid. The direction of the repulsion that he indicated is that his intention is not to make the mentioned division based on its interpretation as arrangement, so that it does not apply to another interpretation according to the doctrine of acquisition. Rather, his intention is that since the chosen [view] among the later scholars is the school of ta'lim – which is the doctrine of arrangement and acquisition – not the doctrine of one who considers nazar as mere turning towards the desired without using information as previously, and after the objective is clear, he does not mind the slightest tolerance in the wording of the matn. And know that nazar – whether we make it the arrangement itself or the movement leading to it – requires sciences arranged in a specific form, that which leads to conceptualization is a definition and to assent is a proof. The sciences, i.e., the present matters, are the matter for that connector, and the specific form is its form, and they may be attributed to nazar by this connection. This is the meaning of the author's statement that every arrangement has a matter and a form; otherwise those sciences and that form are entirely external to thought. By this the aspect of what is said becomes clear: the sciences in which arrangement occurs are like the matter for thought, and the form arranged upon it is like the form. As for the commentator's mention of it in his glosses on al-Mutala' and his small gloss as a justification for that.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the phrase 'ولما كان المختار عند المتأخرين مذهب أهل التعليم' from the matn. The commentator clarifies why the author added the phrase 'school of ta'lim' to the matn. The addition is to prevent confusion: some might think that the division of nazar into valid and invalid is based on its definition as arrangement, but the author's intention is not that. Rather, the chosen view of the later scholars is the school of ta'lim, which affirms both arrangement and acquisition (the idea that new knowledge is acquired from previous knowledge through arrangement), as opposed to the view that nazar is just a direct turning towards the desired without any use of prior information. The commentator then explains that nazar, whether considered as the arrangement itself or the movement leading to it, requires sciences arranged in a specific form. This form serves as a definition for conceptualization and a proof for assent. The sciences present in the mind are the matter, and the specific arrangement is the form. These are attributed to nazar by virtue of this connection. The author's statement that every arrangement has matter and form means that these elements are external to the act of thinking itself. This clarifies the analogy that sciences are like matter for thought and the arrangement is like its form. The commentator notes that he has also discussed this in his glosses on al-Mutala' and his small gloss as a justification.

Misconception & Correction

Correction: The commentator clarifies that the division is independent; the chosen view is the school of ta'lim, which includes arrangement and acquisition, and the division applies regardless.

Checkpoint
What is the purpose of the author adding the phrase 'school of ta'lim' in the matn according to the commentator?
A) To indicate that only the later scholars follow this school.
B) To prevent the misunderstanding that the division of nazar is based on its interpretation as arrangement.
C) To define nazar as mere turning towards the desired.
D) To introduce a new definition of nazar.

Key Takeaway
Nazar, as understood by later scholars, involves arranging sciences in a specific form, with sciences as matter and arrangement as form.

?
When you approach a new question about your faith, do you actively gather and arrange what you already know, or do you expect direct inspiration? How can you practice the discipline of nazar in your daily reasoning about religious matters?
?
The commentator clarifies a subtle misunderstanding to protect the integrity of the argument. Are there theological concepts you hold carelessly? What would it cost you to examine them with this same precision?
?
Your mind is constantly arranging thoughts—what 'matter' are you feeding it, and what 'form' are you imposing? Will your reasoning lead you to true assent (tasdiq) or merely to comfortable conclusions? Commit to one concrete change in how you seek knowledge this week.

Validity and Corruption of Reasoning: Definition and Defense
Defines valid/corrupt reasoning; refutes an objection and a metaphorical interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the criteria for valid and corrupt reasoning (nazar) and how a classic objection about a false syllogism is refuted.

Core Idea
Validity is real, not metaphorical — reasoning either leads to the truth or it doesn't.

Theologians need a clear criterion to distinguish sound reasoning from flawed reasoning. This passage provides that criterion: a valid argument leads to the desired conclusion, while a corrupt one does not. It then defends this definition against an objection that a formally valid but false-premised syllogism would be considered valid, clarifying that real-world truth matters.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of validity and corruption
The passage opens by stating that validity and corruption are real attributes of reasoning. Read carefully how 'leading to the desired conclusion' is the key criterion.
Note the phrase 'not metaphorically' — this is a crucial point.
2
Examine the objection
The objector presents the example 'Zayd is a donkey, every donkey is a body' as a counterexample. Understand why this seems to fit the definition of valid reasoning.
The premises are formally correct, but the first premise is false.
3
Follow the response
The commentator denies that this syllogism actually leads to the conclusion. He explains that the middle term is not truly established for the minor term, so there is no real inclusion.
The response hinges on the reality of the premises, not just their form.
4
Understand the refutation of the metaphorical view
The passage ends by rejecting the idea that validity and corruption are metaphorical divisions, like clear vs. obscure. Ground this in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقصد الثاني : أنه يؤدي إلى المطلوب وفاسد يقابله يقابله أي لا يؤدي إلى المطلوب فالصحة والفساد صفتان عارضتان للنظر حقيقة لا مجازاً، لكنه أراد أن يبين السبب في اتصافه بهما فقال: ولما كان المختار عند المتأخرين مذهب أهل التعليم وهو أنه ترتيب العلوم بحيث يؤدي إلى هيئة مخصوصة. قوله: (يؤدي إلى المطلوب إلخ) قيل يرد على التعريفين قولنا زيد حمار وكل حمار جسم، فإنه يدخل في الصحيح مع أنه فاسد المادة، أقول: لا نسلم تأديته إلى المطلوب، فإن حقيقة القياس على ما صرح به الشارح في حواشيه على شرح المختصر وسط مستلزم للأكبر ثابت للأصغر وهاهنا لا يثبت الأوسط للأصغر فلا اندراج فلا تأدية في نفس الأمر، نعم إنه يؤدي بعد تسليم المقدمتين. قوله: (فالصحة إلخ) رد لما في شرح المقاصد من أن صحة النظر، وفساده عبارة عن صحة مادته وصورته ففي انقسامه إلى الصحيح والفاسد تجوز كما في انقسامه إلى الجلي والخفي.
The second objective: that it leads to the desired [conclusion] and its opposite is corruption. (Its opposite) i.e. it does not lead to the desired [conclusion]. So validity and corruption are two attributes accidental to reasoning (nazar) in reality, not metaphorically. But he wanted to show the reason for its being described by them, so he said: 'And since the chosen [view] according to the later scholars is the school of the people of instruction (madhhab ahl al-ta'lim), which is that it is the arrangement of sciences such that it leads to a specific configuration.' His statement: '(It leads to the desired [conclusion] etc.)' It was said: An objection is raised against both definitions by our saying 'Zayd is a donkey and every donkey is a body,' for it enters into the valid [reasoning] while it is corrupt in matter. I say: We do not accept that it leads to the desired [conclusion], for the reality of the syllogism, according to what the commentator clarified in his glosses on the commentary on al-Mukhtasar (wasat), is that it necessitates the major term being established for the minor, and here the middle term is not established for the minor, so there is no inclusion, so no leading to the [desired conclusion] in reality. Yes, it leads after the two premises are conceded. His statement: '(So validity etc.)' is a refutation of what is in Sharh al-Maqasid: that the validity and corruption of reasoning are expressions of the validity of its matter and form, so in its division into valid and corrupt there is metaphor, as in its division into clear and obscure.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage defines the second objective of the discussion: that theoretical reasoning (nazar) either leads to the desired conclusion (valid) or fails to do so (corrupt). The commentator explains that validity (sihha) and corruption (fasad) are real attributes of reasoning, not metaphorical. He then presents an objection: the statement 'Zayd is a donkey, and every donkey is a body' would be considered valid reasoning under some definitions, but it is corrupt in its matter (since the premise 'Zayd is a donkey' is false). The commentator responds by denying that such a syllogism actually leads to the desired conclusion in reality, because the middle term ('donkey') is not truly affirmed of the minor term ('Zayd'), so there is no proper inclusion. However, he concedes that if the premises were accepted, it would lead formally. Finally, he refutes the view from Sharh al-Maqasid that the division into valid and corrupt is metaphorical, asserting that it is real.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that validity and corruption of reasoning are merely metaphorical descriptions based on matter and form.
Correction: The passage asserts they are real (haqiqa) attributes, not metaphorical (majaz).

Checkpoint
What is the commentator's response to the objection that 'Zayd is a donkey and every donkey is a body' is valid reasoning?
A) He accepts it and considers it valid reasoning.
B) He says it is valid only if the premises are true.
C) He denies that it leads to the desired conclusion because the middle term is not established for the minor term.
D) He says it is valid in form but not in matter.

Key Takeaway
Valid reasoning must not only be formally correct but also have true premises that actually lead to the conclusion in reality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you examine your own reasoning for both formal correctness and truthfulness of premises, or do you assume your arguments are valid because they feel convincing? When was the last time you discovered a flaw in your own reasoning about a religious matter, and how did you respond?
?
This lesson warns that even a formally valid syllogism can be corrupt if its premises are false. In your life, have you ever defended a belief or action using premises that you knew deep down were not true? What would it cost you to commit to truth in your reasoning, even when it means changing your position?
?
If validity of reasoning is real, not metaphorical, then your responsibility to think correctly before God is serious. What specific steps will you take this week to ensure that your reasoning about matters of faith is both sound in form and grounded in truth?

What Is Kalam?

Nazar as Arrangement: The Chosen Definition
Sanusi defines nazar as arrangement and distinguishes it from attention.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the later scholars defined nazar as the arrangement of sciences and how this differs from the view that it is mere attention.

Core Idea
Nazar is not just looking; it is a structured arrangement of known sciences.

The passage begins by establishing the definition of theoretical reasoning (nazar) that became standard among later Sunni theologians. It explains that they adopted the view of the 'people of instruction' (ahl al-ta'lim), who see nazar as a deliberate arrangement of previously known sciences to reach a new conclusion. This definition sets the stage for analyzing the components of valid reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of nazar
Read the passage and identify the definition of nazar as 'arrangement of sciences'. Note that the commentator adds the phrase 'school of the people of instruction' to clarify that this is the chosen view.
The definition is presented as the chosen view of the later scholars.
2
Contrast with other views
Notice that the passage distinguishes this definition from the view that nazar is mere attention (tawajjuh) towards the desired conclusion without using prior knowledge.
The contrast highlights the necessity of using known sciences.
3
Understand the purpose of the addition
The commentator adds 'school of the people of instruction' to prevent misunderstanding that the division of nazar into valid and corrupt depends solely on the arrangement interpretation. It also emphasizes the role of acquisition (iktisab).
This clarifies that the definition is not merely arrangement but arrangement plus acquisition.

الاستلزام الكلي لا ينفع لتحققه في خصوص أمثال المذكور، ونظائره كما لا يخفى ثم المطلوب الاعتقاد المطابق علماً أو ظناً. هو قوله : ( ولما كان المختار عند المتأخرين مذهب أهل التعليم، وهو أنه ترتيب العلوم عبارة المتن هكذا ولما كان المختار أنه ترتيب العلوم فزاد الشارح قوله مذهب أهل التعليم إشارة إلى دفع ما يتوهم من ظاهر عبارته من ابتناء انقسام النظر إلى الصحيح والفاسد على تفسيره بالترتيب كما ذكره شارح التعليم وهو القول بالترتيب والاكتساب دون مذهب من يرى النظر مجرد التوجه إلى المطلوب من غير استعانة بمعلومات كما سبق، وبعد وضوح المقصود لا يبالي بما في عبارة المتن من أدنى مسامحة، واعلم أن النظر سواء جعلناه نفس الترتيب أو الحركة المفضية إليه يستدعي علوما مرتبة على هيئة مخصوصة الموصل منها إلى التصور معرفاً وإلى التصديق دليلاً، ويكون العلوم أي الأمور الحاضرة مادة لذلك الموصل، والهيئة المخصوصة صورة له وقد يضافان إلى النظر بهذه الملابسة، وهذا معنى كلام المصنف أن لكل ترتيب مادة وصورة وإلا فتلك العلوم وتلك الهيئة خارجتان عن الفكر قطعاً، وبهذا يظهر وجه ما يقال: إن العلوم التي يقع فيها الترتيب بمنزلة المادة للفكر، والهيئة المترتبة عليه بمنزلة الصورة، وأما ذكره الشارح في حواشي المطالع وحاشيته الصغرى توجيهاً لذلك القول أن الفكر عرض لا مادة له ولا صورة، ففيه بحث لأن المفهوم من إطلاقاتهم في مباحث العلة والمعلول عموم العلة الصورية والمادية بحسب الاصطلاح للجواهر والأعراض كما سيأتي إن شاء الله. لتأدي إلى مجهول ولا شك أن هذا الترتيب يتعلق بشيئين أحدهما تلك العلوم التي يقع فيها الترتيب وهي بمنزلة المادة له والثاني تلك الهيئة المترتبة عليه وهي بمنزلة الصورة له، فإذا اتصف كل واحدة منهما بما هو صحتها في نفسها اتصف الترتيب قطعاً بصحته في نفسه، أعني تأديته إلى المطلوب، وإلا فلا وهذا معنى قوله ( ولكل ترتيب مادة وصورة أي لا بد له من أمرين يجريان منه مجرى المادة والصورة من ) المركب منهما ( فتكون ) جواب لما الفاء مع وهو قليل في الاستعمال (صحته ) أي صحة النظر بمعنى تأديته إلى المطلوب ) بصحة المادة ) أي بسبب صحتها، أما في التصورات فمثل أن يكون المذكور في موضع الجنس مثلاً جنساً لا عرضاً عاماً، وفي موضع الفصل فصلا لا خاصة وفي موضع الخاصة خاصة شاملة بينة، وأما في التصديقات فمثل أن تكون القضايا المذكورة في الدليل مناسبة للمطلوب وصادقة إما . قوله : ( ولا شك إلخ ) أي هذا الترتيب الذي هو فعل الناظر يتعلق بشيئين أحدهما بمنزلة المادة في كون الترتيب به بالقوة والثاني بمنزلة الصورة في حصوله به بالفعل، فإذا اتصف كل واحد بما هو صحته في نفسه اتصف الترتيب بالصحة التي هي صفته بخلاف ما إذا كان عبارة عن الحركتين، لأن الحركة حاصلة بالفعل من مبدأ المسافة أعني المطلوب المشعور به بوجه إلى منتهاها أعني الوجه المجهول وليست بالقوة عند حصول العلوم، وبالفعل عند حصول الهيئة فلا تكون صحة النظر، حينئذ بصحة المادة والصورة بل بترتب ما لأجله الحركة أعني حصول العلوم المناسبة والهيئة المنتجة وبخلاف ما إذا كان عبارة عن التوجه المذكور فإن العلوم السابقة لا مدخل لها في التأدية حينئذ، فلا تكون صحته لصحة المادة والصورة أيضا، وبما ذكرنا اندفع ما في شرح المقاصد من أنه يستفاد من عبارة المواقف ابتناء انقسام النظر إلى الصحيح والفاسد، باعتبار المادة والصورة على تفسيره بالترتيب وليس كذلك ولبعض الناظرين لبيان الابتناء المذكور توجيه بعيد عن العبارة لا يقبله الطبع السليم.
The universal implication does not benefit because it holds specifically in such examples and their likes, as is not hidden. Then the desired [conclusion] is belief that corresponds [to reality], knowledge or conjecture. He says: 'And since the chosen [view] according to the later scholars is the school of the people of instruction (madhhab ahl al-ta'lim), which is that it is the arrangement of sciences' — the text of the matn is thus: 'And since the chosen [view] is that it is the arrangement of sciences.' So the commentator added his statement 'the school of the people of instruction' as an indication to repel what might be imagined from the apparent meaning of his statement, that the division of reasoning (nazar) into valid and corrupt is based on its interpretation as arrangement, as mentioned by the commentator of al-Maqasid. The way of repelling that he indicated is that his intention is not to make the mentioned division based on its interpretation as arrangement, so that it would not run on another interpretation according to the theory of acquisition (iktisab). Rather, his intention is that since the chosen [view] according to the later scholars is the school of the people of instruction — which is the statement of arrangement and acquisition, not the school of one who considers reasoning mere attention (tawajjuh) towards the desired [conclusion] without the aid of known things, as previously — and after the clarification of the intended meaning, he does not mind any slight looseness in the text of the matn. Know that reasoning, whether we make it the arrangement itself or the movement leading to it, requires sciences arranged in a specific configuration (hay'a makhsusa), the means of which to conception (tasawwur) is a definition (mu'arraf) and to assent (tasdiq) is a proof (dalil). The sciences — i.e., the present matters — are the matter (madda) for that means, and the specific configuration is its form (sura); and they may be attributed to reasoning by this relation. This is the meaning of the author's statement: 'Every arrangement has matter and form'; otherwise, those sciences and that configuration are completely external to thought. By this appears the face of what is said: that the sciences in which the arrangement occurs are like matter for thought, and the configuration arranged upon them is like form. As for the commentator's mention in his glosses on al-Matali' and his small gloss as a justification for that statement — that thought (fikr) is an accident with no matter or form — there is discussion in it, because the understanding from their usages in the topics of cause and effect is the generality of formal and material cause in terminology to substances and accidents, as will come, God willing. Leading to the unknown. There is no doubt that this arrangement is related to two things: one of them is those sciences in which the arrangement occurs, and they are like matter for it; the second is that configuration arranged upon them, and it is like form for it. So when each of them is described by what is its validity in itself, the arrangement is certainly described by its validity in itself, i.e., its leading to the desired [conclusion]; otherwise not. This is the meaning of his statement: 'And every arrangement has matter and form' — i.e., it must have two things that proceed from it like matter and form from what is composed of them. Then (fa-takun) is the answer to a conditional, with the fa' and it is rare in usage. 'Its validity' (sihhatuhu) i.e., the validity of reasoning in the sense of its leading to the desired [conclusion] 'by the validity of the matter' (bi-sihhat al-madda) i.e., because of its validity. As for conceptions (tasawwurat), for example, that what is mentioned in the place of genus be a genus, not a general accident; in the place of differentia be a differentia, not a property; in the place of property (khassa) be a comprehensive evident property. As for assents (tasdiqat), for example, that the propositions mentioned in the proof be appropriate for the desired [conclusion] and true, either ... . His statement: '(And there is no doubt etc.)' i.e., this arrangement, which is the act of the reasoner, is related to two things: one of them is like matter in that the arrangement is potential by it, and the second is like form in its actualization by it. So when each one is described by what is its validity in itself, the arrangement is described by the validity that is its attribute, contrary to when it is an expression of the two movements, because movement is already actual from the beginning of the distance — i.e., the desired [conclusion] known in some way — to its end — i.e., the unknown aspect — and it is not potential at the time of obtaining the sciences, but actual at the time of obtaining the configuration. Then the validity of reasoning would not be due to the validity of matter and form, but by the arrangement for whose sake the movement occurs — i.e., obtaining the appropriate sciences and the productive configuration. And contrary to when it is an expression of the mentioned attention (tawajjuh), for then the prior sciences have no entry into leading [to the conclusion], so its validity is also not due to the validity of matter and form. By what we have mentioned, what is in Sharh al-Maqasid is repelled: that from the wording of al-Mawaqif it is understood that the division of reasoning into valid and corrupt, considering matter and form, is based on its interpretation as arrangement; it is not so. And some reasoners have for explaining that grounding a justification far from the wording, which a sound disposition does not accept.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of the nature of theoretical reasoning (nazar) as defined by the later scholars (muta'akhkhirin) — the school of ahl al-ta'lim, which holds that nazar is the arrangement of sciences that leads to a specific configuration. The commentator first addresses an objection about universal implication, then clarifies that the intended definition is not merely arrangement, but arrangement coupled with acquisition (iktisab), distinguishing it from the view that nazar is mere attention. He then explains that every arrangement must have both matter (the sciences themselves) and form (the specific configuration). The matter is the raw material, and the form is the structure that yields a definition for conceptions or a proof for assents. The commentator emphasizes that both matter and form are essential: if either is unsound, the arrangement does not actually lead to the desired conclusion. He provides examples for both conceptions (tasawwurat) and assents (tasdiqat). Finally, he contrasts this view with two other definitions of nazar: as movement (haraka) and as mere attention (tawajjuh). In the movement view, validity depends on the order of the movement rather than directly on matter and form. In the attention view, prior sciences are irrelevant. Thus, the division of nazar into valid and corrupt based on matter and form is only fully appropriate when nazar is understood as arrangement. The commentator concludes by refuting the suggestion from Sharh al-Maqasid that the division is based on the arrangement interpretation, asserting that other interpretations do not yield the same division.

Key Terms
ترتيب
اكتساب
توجه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That nazar is simply any mental attention towards a desired conclusion without requiring prior knowledge or structure.
Correction: The passage clarifies that nazar is a specific arrangement of sciences, not mere attention, and that it requires both arrangement and acquisition.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the chosen definition of nazar among later scholars?
A) Mere attention towards the desired conclusion.
B) The arrangement of sciences with acquisition.
C) The movement of the soul from known to unknown.
D) The universal implication of known truths.

Key Takeaway
Nazar is defined as the arrangement of sciences with acquisition, contrasting with mere attention.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a difficult theological question, do you instinctively rely on memorized answers or do you deliberately arrange known principles to reason through it? Are you willing to do the hard work of tartib, or do you prefer the comfort of tawajjuh?
?
This lesson distinguishes between mere attention and structured reasoning. Where in your own life do you catch yourself 'just paying attention' to your deen without actually engaging your mind and prior knowledge? Will you commit to moving from passive attention to active arrangement?
?
The commentator added a clarification to prevent misunderstanding. Are there areas of your faith where you have accepted a simplistic definition without probing its deeper implications? Will you take time today to ask an 'ugly question' about a concept you thought you understood?

What Is Kalam?

Matter, Form, and Validity of Reasoning
Sanusi explains matter and form of reasoning and how they affect validity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that every arrangement of reasoning has matter (the sciences) and form (the specific configuration), and that the soundness of reasoning depends on the soundness of both matter and form.

Core Idea
Valid reasoning needs both correct facts (matter) and logical structure (form).

Having established nazar as arrangement, the passage now unpacks its components. Every arrangement, the commentator argues, must have matter (the sciences that are arranged) and form (the specific configuration that organizes them). Just as a physical object needs both material and shape, reasoning needs correct premises and a valid logical structure. The passage gives examples for conceptions and assents, then contrasts this view with alternative definitions of nazar.

Guided Path
1
Identify matter and form
Read the passage and find the explicit statement that every arrangement has matter and form. Note that the matter is the sciences themselves and the form is the specific configuration (hay'a).
The author asserts that without both, the arrangement cannot fulfill its purpose.
2
See how validity depends on both
The passage explains that if both matter and form are sound in themselves, the arrangement is sound, leading to the desired conclusion. Examples are given for conceptions (tasawwurat) and assents (tasdiqat).
For example, in a definition, the genus must be a true genus, the differentia a true differentia.
3
Contrast with other definitions
The passage contrasts this view with two other definitions of nazar: as movement (haraka) and as mere attention (tawajjuh). In those views, validity does not directly depend on matter and form as described.
This reinforces that the matter-form analysis is specific to the arrangement definition.

المادة للفكر، والهيئة المترتبة عليه بمنزلة الصورة، وأما ذكره الشارح في حواشي المطالع وحاشيته الصغرى توجيهاً لذلك القول أن الفكر عرض لا مادة له ولا صورة، ففيه بحث لأن المفهوم من إطلاقاتهم في مباحث العلة والمعلول عموم العلة الصورية والمادية بحسب الاصطلاح للجواهر والأعراض كما سيأتي إن شاء الله. لتأدي إلى مجهول ولا شك أن هذا الترتيب يتعلق بشيئين أحدهما تلك العلوم التي يقع فيها الترتيب وهي بمنزلة المادة له والثاني تلك الهيئة المترتبة عليه وهي بمنزلة الصورة له، فإذا اتصف كل واحدة منهما بما هو صحتها في نفسها اتصف الترتيب قطعاً بصحته في نفسه، أعني تأديته إلى المطلوب، وإلا فلا وهذا معنى قوله ( ولكل ترتيب مادة وصورة أي لا بد له من أمرين يجريان منه مجرى المادة والصورة من ) المركب منهما ( فتكون ) جواب لما الفاء مع وهو قليل في الاستعمال (صحته ) أي صحة النظر بمعنى تأديته إلى المطلوب ) بصحة المادة ) أي بسبب صحتها، أما في التصورات فمثل أن يكون المذكور في موضع الجنس مثلاً جنساً لا عرضاً عاماً، وفي موضع الفصل فصلا لا خاصة وفي موضع الخاصة خاصة شاملة بينة، وأما في التصديقات فمثل أن تكون القضايا المذكورة في الدليل مناسبة للمطلوب وصادقة إما . قوله : ( ولا شك إلخ ) أي هذا الترتيب الذي هو فعل الناظر يتعلق بشيئين أحدهما بمنزلة المادة في كون الترتيب به بالقوة والثاني بمنزلة الصورة في حصوله به بالفعل، فإذا اتصف كل واحد بما هو صحته في نفسه اتصف الترتيب بالصحة التي هي صفته بخلاف ما إذا كان عبارة عن الحركتين، لأن الحركة حاصلة بالفعل من مبدأ المسافة أعني المطلوب المشعور به بوجه إلى منتهاها أعني الوجه المجهول وليست بالقوة عند حصول العلوم، وبالفعل عند حصول الهيئة فلا تكون صحة النظر، حينئذ بصحة المادة والصورة بل بترتب ما لأجله الحركة أعني حصول العلوم المناسبة والهيئة المنتجة وبخلاف ما إذا كان عبارة عن التوجه المذكور فإن العلوم السابقة لا مدخل لها في التأدية حينئذ، فلا تكون صحته لصحة المادة والصورة أيضا، وبما ذكرنا اندفع ما في شرح المقاصد من أنه يستفاد من عبارة المواقف ابتناء انقسام النظر إلى الصحيح والفاسد، باعتبار المادة والصورة على تفسيره بالترتيب وليس كذلك ولبعض الناظرين لبيان الابتناء المذكور توجيه بعيد عن العبارة لا يقبله الطبع السليم.
The universal implication does not benefit because it holds specifically in such examples and their likes, as is not hidden. Then the desired [conclusion] is belief that corresponds [to reality], knowledge or conjecture. He says: 'And since the chosen [view] according to the later scholars is the school of the people of instruction (madhhab ahl al-ta'lim), which is that it is the arrangement of sciences' — the text of the matn is thus: 'And since the chosen [view] is that it is the arrangement of sciences.' So the commentator added his statement 'the school of the people of instruction' as an indication to repel what might be imagined from the apparent meaning of his statement, that the division of reasoning (nazar) into valid and corrupt is based on its interpretation as arrangement, as mentioned by the commentator of al-Maqasid. The way of repelling that he indicated is that his intention is not to make the mentioned division based on its interpretation as arrangement, so that it would not run on another interpretation according to the theory of acquisition (iktisab). Rather, his intention is that since the chosen [view] according to the later scholars is the school of the people of instruction — which is the statement of arrangement and acquisition, not the school of one who considers reasoning mere attention (tawajjuh) towards the desired [conclusion] without the aid of known things, as previously — and after the clarification of the intended meaning, he does not mind any slight looseness in the text of the matn. Know that reasoning, whether we make it the arrangement itself or the movement leading to it, requires sciences arranged in a specific configuration (hay'a makhsusa), the means of which to conception (tasawwur) is a definition (mu'arraf) and to assent (tasdiq) is a proof (dalil). The sciences — i.e., the present matters — are the matter (madda) for that means, and the specific configuration is its form (sura); and they may be attributed to reasoning by this relation. This is the meaning of the author's statement: 'Every arrangement has matter and form'; otherwise, those sciences and that configuration are completely external to thought. By this appears the face of what is said: that the sciences in which the arrangement occurs are like matter for thought, and the configuration arranged upon them is like form. As for the commentator's mention in his glosses on al-Matali' and his small gloss as a justification for that statement — that thought (fikr) is an accident with no matter or form — there is discussion in it, because the understanding from their usages in the topics of cause and effect is the generality of formal and material cause in terminology to substances and accidents, as will come, God willing. Leading to the unknown. There is no doubt that this arrangement is related to two things: one of them is those sciences in which the arrangement occurs, and they are like matter for it; the second is that configuration arranged upon them, and it is like form for it. So when each of them is described by what is its validity in itself, the arrangement is certainly described by its validity in itself, i.e., its leading to the desired [conclusion]; otherwise not. This is the meaning of his statement: 'And every arrangement has matter and form' — i.e., it must have two things that proceed from it like matter and form from what is composed of them. Then (fa-takun) is the answer to a conditional, with the fa' and it is rare in usage. 'Its validity' (sihhatuhu) i.e., the validity of reasoning in the sense of its leading to the desired [conclusion] 'by the validity of the matter' (bi-sihhat al-madda) i.e., because of its validity. As for conceptions (tasawwurat), for example, that what is mentioned in the place of genus be a genus, not a general accident; in the place of differentia be a differentia, not a property; in the place of property (khassa) be a comprehensive evident property. As for assents (tasdiqat), for example, that the propositions mentioned in the proof be appropriate for the desired [conclusion] and true, either ... . His statement: '(And there is no doubt etc.)' i.e., this arrangement, which is the act of the reasoner, is related to two things: one of them is like matter in that the arrangement is potential by it, and the second is like form in its actualization by it. So when each one is described by what is its validity in itself, the arrangement is described by the validity that is its attribute, contrary to when it is an expression of the two movements, because movement is already actual from the beginning of the distance — i.e., the desired [conclusion] known in some way — to its end — i.e., the unknown aspect — and it is not potential at the time of obtaining the sciences, but actual at the time of obtaining the configuration. Then the validity of reasoning would not be due to the validity of matter and form, but by the arrangement for whose sake the movement occurs — i.e., obtaining the appropriate sciences and the productive configuration. And contrary to when it is an expression of the mentioned attention (tawajjuh), for then the prior sciences have no entry into leading [to the conclusion], so its validity is also not due to the validity of matter and form. By what we have mentioned, what is in Sharh al-Maqasid is repelled: that from the wording of al-Mawaqif it is understood that the division of reasoning into valid and corrupt, considering matter and form, is based on its interpretation as arrangement; it is not so. And some reasoners have for explaining that grounding a justification far from the wording, which a sound disposition does not accept.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of the nature of theoretical reasoning (nazar) as defined by the later scholars (muta'akhkhirin) — the school of ahl al-ta'lim, which holds that nazar is the arrangement of sciences that leads to a specific configuration. The commentator first addresses an objection about universal implication, then clarifies that the intended definition is not merely arrangement, but arrangement coupled with acquisition (iktisab), distinguishing it from the view that nazar is mere attention. He then explains that every arrangement must have both matter (the sciences themselves) and form (the specific configuration). The matter is the raw material, and the form is the structure that yields a definition for conceptions or a proof for assents. The commentator emphasizes that both matter and form are essential: if either is unsound, the arrangement does not actually lead to the desired conclusion. He provides examples for both conceptions (tasawwurat) and assents (tasdiqat). Finally, he contrasts this view with two other definitions of nazar: as movement (haraka) and as mere attention (tawajjuh). In the movement view, validity depends on the order of the movement rather than directly on matter and form. In the attention view, prior sciences are irrelevant. Thus, the division of nazar into valid and corrupt based on matter and form is only fully appropriate when nazar is understood as arrangement. The commentator concludes by refuting the suggestion from Sharh al-Maqasid that the division is based on the arrangement interpretation, asserting that other interpretations do not yield the same division.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the division of nazar into valid and corrupt applies to all definitions of nazar.
Correction: The passage shows that this division is specific to the arrangement definition; other definitions have different criteria for validity.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what determines the validity of reasoning as arrangement?
A) The soundness of the arrangement's matter only.
B) The soundness of the arrangement's form only.
C) The soundness of both matter and form.
D) The number of sciences used.

Key Takeaway
Valid reasoning (nazar) as arrangement requires sound matter and sound form; this distinguishes it from other definitions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your own study of 'aqeedah, do you examine both the truth of your premises (matter) and the structure of your arguments (form)? Which do you tend to neglect, and how might that be leading you to error without you realizing it?
?
The commentator warns that reasoning can be valid or corrupt based on matter and form. Is there a belief you hold that you have never critically examined in terms of its logical structure? Will you take the time today to analyze its form, or are you content with assuming it is correct because its premises are true?
?
When you engage in reasoning about Allah, are you seeking only to confirm what you already know, or are you willing to test the soundness of both your information and your reasoning? What would change in your practice of faith if you took this lesson seriously?

What Is Kalam?
intermediate
4 min
Nazar as Tartib: Matter and Form
The commentator defines nazar as a tartib and identifies its matter and form.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that nazar (reasoning) is defined as a specific ordering (tartib) that has two essential components: matter (the premises) and form (the arrangement).

Core Idea
Reasoning is an ordering with matter and form — like a body.

In this passage, the commentator lays the foundation for understanding sound reasoning. He introduces nazar as a tartib, an ordering that relates to two things: the sciences that serve as raw material (matter) and the way they are arranged (form). This idea is central to the entire discipline of logic and kalam.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the two components
Read the Arabic text and translation carefully. Notice the two things: sciences and arrangement. They are likened to matter and form.
2
Understand the condition for soundness
The text states that when each component is sound, the ordering is sound. Ask yourself why both are necessary.
This is a key condition.
3
Recognize the meaning of the statement
The passage explains the phrase 'every ordering has matter and form' and the grammatical point about 'ba'. This is a key technical point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الخامس - المقصد الثاني : أنه يؤدي إلى المطلوب وفاسد يقابله لتأدي إلى مجهول ولا شك أن هذا الترتيب يتعلق بشيئين أحدهما تلك العلوم التي يقع فيها الترتيب وهي بمنزلة المادة له والثاني تلك الهيئة المترتبة عليه وهي بمنزلة الصورة له، فإذا اتصف كل واحدة منهما بما هو صحتها في نفسها اتصف الترتيب قطعاً بصحته في نفسه، أعني تأديته إلى المطلوب، وإلا فلا وهذا معنى قوله ( ولكل ترتيب مادة وصورة أي لا بد التصورات فمثل أن يكون المذكور في موضع الجنس مثلاً جنساً لا عرضاً عاماً، وفي موضع الفصل فصلا لا خاصة وفي موضع الخاصة خاصة شاملة بينة، وأما في التصديقات فمثل أن تكون القضايا المذكورة في الدليل مناسبة للمطلوب وصادقة إما قوله : ( ولا شك إلخ ) أي هذا الترتيب الذي هو فعل الناظر يتعلق بشيئين أحدهما بمنزلة المادة في كون الترتيب به بالقوة والثاني بمنزلة الصورة في حصوله به بالفعل، فإذا اتصف كل واحد بما هو صحته في نفسه اتصف الترتيب بالصحة التي هي صفته بخلاف ما إذا كان عبارة عن الحركتين، لأن الحركة حاصلة بالفعل من مبدأ المسافة أعني المطلوب المشعور به بوجه إلى منتهاها أعني الوجه المجهول وليست بالقوة عند حصول العلوم، وبالفعل عند حصول الهيئة فلا تكون صحة النظر، حينئذ بصحة المادة والصورة بل بترتب ما لأجله الحركة أعني حصول العلوم المناسبة والهيئة المنتجة وبخلاف ما إذا كان عبارة عن التوجه المذكور فإن العلوم السابقة لا مدخل لها في التأدية حينئذ، فلا تكون صحته لصحة المادة والصورة أيضا، وبما ذكرنا اندفع ما في شرح المقاصد من أنه يستفاد من عبارة المواقف ابتناء انقسام النظر إلى الصحيح والفاسد، باعتبار المادة والصورة على تفسيره بالترتيب وليس كذلك ولبعض الناظرين لبيان الابتناء المذكور توجيه بعيد عن العبارة لا يقبله الطبع السليم. قوله : ( وهي بمنزلة المادة إلخ ) زاد لفظ بمنزلة لعدم كونهما ركنين للترتيب، ولأن المادة والصورة مختصة بالأجسام، والوجه الأخير ذكره الشارح في حاشيته الكبرى والصغرى، التخصيص مستنداً بأن العلة المادية والصورية شاملة للجواهر والأعراض، منشؤه والاعتراض بمنع عدم الفرق بين المادة والصورة والعلة المادية والصورية فلا تكن من الخابطين. قوله : (بسبب صحتها يعني أن الباء للسببية لا للملابسة، حتى يكون المعنى صحته باعتبار صحتها فيكون وصفه بها باعتبار حال متعلقه أي صحيح مادتها وصورتها على ما في شرح المقاصد . وحاشيته الصغرى توجيهاً لذلك القول أن الفكر عرض لا مادة له ولا صورة، ففيه بحث لأن المفهوم من إطلاقاتهم في مباحث العلة والمعلول عموم العلة الصورية والمادية بحسب الاصطلاح للجواهر والأعراض كما سيأتي إن شاء الله . المرصد الخامس - المقصد الثاني : أنه يؤدي إلى المطلوب وفاسد يقابله ٢١٣ قوله : (إما قطعاً إلخ) مفعول مطلق أي صدق قطع أو ظن أو تسليم أو حال، أي مقطوعة أو مظنونة أو مسلمة وهذا تقسيم باعتبار الصناعات الثلاثة المعتبرة في تحصيل المطالب النظرية، أعني البرهان والخطابة والجدل وأسقط المغالطة والشعر لعدم إفادتهما المجهول . قوله : (مجتمعتين) إشارة إلى أن كلمة معاً حال وليس ظرفاً بمعنى في وقت واحد .
The fifth observatory - the second objective: that it (nazar) leads to the desired conclusion and its opposite is unsound. For it leads to the unknown. There is no doubt that this ordering (tartib) relates to two things: one is those sciences in which the ordering occurs, and they are like the matter (madda) for it; the second is that arrangement (hay'a) which is ordered upon it, and it is like the form (sura) for it. When each of them is characterized by what is its soundness in itself, the ordering is necessarily characterized by its own soundness, i.e., its leading to the desired conclusion; otherwise not. This is the meaning of his statement: (And every ordering has matter and form, i.e., it must have two things that proceed from it in the manner of matter and form from the composite of both. So (it becomes) the answer to 'lam' with 'fa'—and its usage is rare— (its soundness) i.e., the soundness of nazar in the sense of its leading to the desired (conclusion) (by the soundness of the matter) i.e., due to its soundness. As for conceptions (tasawwurat), for example, that what is mentioned in the place of the genus is a genus, not a common accident; and in the place of the differentia, it is a differentia, not a proprium; and in the place of the proprium, it is a comprehensive and evident proprium. As for assents (tasdiqat), for example, that the propositions mentioned in the proof (dalil) are appropriate to the desired conclusion and true, either... His statement: (And there is no doubt, etc.) i.e., this ordering, which is the act of the inquirer (nazir), relates to two things: one is in the position of matter in that the ordering is potential through it; the second is in the position of form in that it is actualized through it. When each is characterized by what is its soundness in itself, the ordering is characterized by the soundness that is its attribute, unlike if it were expressed by two movements, because the movement is actually obtained from the starting point of the distance, i.e., the desired known in some way, to its endpoint, i.e., the unknown face, and it is not potential when the sciences are obtained, but actual when the arrangement is obtained. Thus, the soundness of nazar then is not due to the soundness of matter and form, but rather due to the ordering for the sake of which the movement occurs, i.e., the obtaining of appropriate sciences and the productive arrangement. And unlike if it were expressed by the aforementioned attention (tawajjuh), for the prior sciences have no role in the leading then; hence its soundness is not due to the soundness of matter and form either. By what we have mentioned, what is in Sharh al-Maqasid is refuted: that it is understood from the expression of al-Mawaqif that the division of nazar into sound and unsound is based on matter and form according to its interpretation as ordering, and this is not so. Some inquirers, to clarify the aforementioned foundation, have a direction far from the expression that a sound disposition does not accept. His statement: (And they are in the position of matter, etc.) He added the word 'position' (bi-manzila) because they are not pillars (rukn) for the ordering, and because matter and form are specific to bodies. The latter point was mentioned by the commentator in his major and minor glosses, the specification being based on the fact that material and formal causes encompass substances and accidents. Its origin and the objection by denying the difference between matter and form and material and formal cause—so do not be among the confused. His statement: (due to its soundness) means that the 'ba' is for causality, not for accompaniment, so that the meaning is: its soundness by virtue of its soundness, so its description is by virtue of the state of its object, i.e., its matter and form are sound, as in Sharh al-Maqasid and his minor gloss, as a direction for that statement: that thought (fikr) is an accident with no matter or form. In it there is investigation because the understood from their usages in the topics of cause and effect is the generality of formal and material cause in terminology for substances and accidents, as will come, God willing. The fifth observatory - the second objective: that it (nazar) leads to the desired conclusion and its opposite is unsound. His statement: (either qat'an, etc.) is an absolute object, i.e., truth of certainty (qat'), or opinion (zann), or concession (taslim), or a state, i.e., being certain, opined, or conceded. This is a division according to the three arts (sina'at) considered in obtaining theoretical aims, namely demonstration (burhan), oratory (khataba), and dialectic (jadal). He omitted sophistry (mugalata) and poetry (shi'r) because they do not benefit the unknown. His statement: (both together (ma'an)) indicates that the word 'ma'an' is a state (hal) and not an adverb meaning 'at one time'.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage is a definition-and-condition passage. The commentator explains the nature of correct reasoning (nazar) as an ordering (tartib) that leads from known premises to an unknown conclusion. He identifies two essential components of this ordering: the matter (madda), which consists of the sciences (premises) that serve as raw material, and the form (sura), which is the arrangement (hay'a) of those premises. The soundness (sihha) of the reasoning depends on the soundness of both matter and form. If either is corrupt (fasid), the reasoning is unsound. The commentator then discusses the types of premises: they must be true either by certainty (qat'), opinion (zann), or concession (taslim), corresponding to the three arts of demonstration, oratory, and dialectic. He also refutes an interpretation that nazar's soundness is based on movement or attention, emphasizing instead the interdependence of matter and form. Finally, he clarifies that the word 'ma'an' (together) in the phrase 'بسبب صحتها معاً' indicates a state, not a temporal adverb.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think nazar is merely a mental act without structure.
Correction: The passage emphasizes it is a tartib with both material and formal components.

Checkpoint
What are the two components of nazar mentioned in this passage?
A) Matter and form
B) Known and unknown
C) Certain and opinion
D) Syllogism and induction

Key Takeaway
Nazar is an ordering with two essential components: matter (premises) and form (arrangement), and its soundness requires both to be sound.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reason about matters of faith, do you consciously examine both the content (the truths you start from) and the structure (how you connect them) as this passage defines? What evidence do you have that you do this regularly?
?
If your reasoning leads to a conclusion that feels shaky, which component do you usually suspect first — the premises or the arrangement? How does this passage challenge you to check both equally?
?
This passage says soundness depends on both matter and form. Think of a time you were convinced of something but couldn't explain it clearly. Did that expose a weakness in your form? How will you train yourself to strengthen both before you speak?
